SEMESTER: S5 
TYRE TECHNOLOGY 
Course Code 
PBPOT504 
CIE Marks 
60 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Basic Knowledge in 
Rubbers
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To explain the Industrial manufacturing of tyres along with its research and development 
2. 
To introduce students about the machineries used to manufacture various types of tyres and also 
the formulation for various tyre components, its processing, building and curing process. 
3. 
After this course the student will be able to explain the tyre grip mechanism, tyre design features 
and tyre testing methods 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to tyres: Tyre functions, History on the design and development 
of tyres, current status of tyre industry in India and its future prospects, tyre 
sizing, different components of a tyre, its geometry, basic functions, functions 
of a pneumatic tyre, load carrying, vibration and noise reduction, the tyre 
function as a spring, contribution to road adhesion, tyre friction contribution 
to driving control, steering control and self-aligning torque. Solid tyres, 
concave tyres, winter tyres, OTR tyre, bicycle tyre, different types of tyres, 
bias, bias belted, radial, relative merits and demerits, their components, tube 
and tubeless tyres basic features. 
11 
2 
Manufacturing techniques of various tyres - two-wheeler, car tyres, truck 
tyres, cycle tyres, cycle tubes, OTR tyres, aircraft tyres, automotive tubes, 
manufacture of tyre treads, beads, sidewalls, compounding techniques, 
principles of designing formulations for various rubber components, tyre 
11 

 
 
reinforcement materials (textile, steel, glass, aramid), criteria of selection, 
different styles and construction, textile treatment (RFL dip). 
3 
Tyre mould design- green tyre design principles, methods of building green 
tyres for bias, bias belted, radial and tubeless tyres, green tyre treatments, tyre 
curing methods, curing bags, bladders, diaphragms, autoclave, airbag, 
bagomatic, autoform, post cure inflation, different types of tyre building 
machines, bead winding machine, bias cutters, curing presses. 
11 
4 
Tyre Testing and Quality Control- Measurement of tyre properties, 
dimension and size-static and loaded, tyre construction analysis, endurance 
test, wheel and plunger tests, traction, cornering coefficient aligning torque 
coefficient, rolling resistance, non-uniformity dimensional variations, force 
variations, radial force variation, lateral force variation concentricity and ply 
steer, tyre balance, mileage, X-ray holography, foot print pressure distribution, 
BIS standards for tyres, tubes and flaps, quality control tests, failure 
mechanism of cord reinforced rubber, tyre forces on dry and wet road surface, 
traction forces on dry, wet, ice, snow and irregular pavements, tyre noise, 
mechanism 
of 
noise 
generation, 
flatspotting, 
fatigue 
resistance, 
pantographing, pneumatic resilience effect. 
11 
 
Suggestion on Project Topics 
● 
After teaching the students the fundamentals of Tyre Technology (Module 1) 
● 
Faculty can direct the students to design a tyre according to a particular need.  
● 
Ensure that it is suitable for the course.  
● 
Students should prepare the plan which includes the appropriate compounding ingredients 
and formulations for various tyre components in the due time of Module II. 
● 
Students can refer the appropriate code of practices.  
● 
Students can fabricate different components of tyre with the help of suitable machineries. 
● 
Assembling of tyres and curing of tyres should also be done according to the tyre type in 
the due period of Module III. 
● 
Any tyre testing methods can also be performed by the student on the tyre he/she has 
designed during the time of Module IV. 

 
 
● 
Students should submit the report to the faculty.

SEMESTER: S5 
ENGINEERING STATISTICS AND QUALITY CONTROL 
Course Code 
PEPOT521 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To introduce various statistical testing methods  
2. To familiarize about the process of quality checking 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Population and sampling: - large and small samples, random sampling, 
stratified sampling, estimating the mean and variance, confidence intervals, 
choice of sample size for estimation. 
9  
2 
Testing of hypotheses for large samples: - means, proportions, difference 
of means and standard deviations. Testing of hypothesis for small samples, t-
distribution, test of hypothesis for mean, difference of means, test for paired 
data, F-distribution, f-tests and properties, contingency table, χ 2 distribution, 
goodness of fit and independence of attributes. 
9  
3 
Meaning of quality, variables and attributes data: - benefits of control 
charts, 
control 
charts 
for 
variables, 
check 
list 
for 
 and R charts, calculation of 3-sigma limits for   , control charts for range, 
OC curve for chart, OC curve for R chart, average run length (ARL) for the 
 chart. Control charts for fraction rejected, control chart for attributes, 
9  

 
 
control limit for the p-chart, control chart for non-conformities, c-chart in 
statistical process control, applications of c chart, limits for c-chart 
4 
Acceptance sample: - types of acceptance, sampling plans, determination of 
probability of acceptance by these sampling plans, sampling risks, design of 
sampling for stipulated producers risk and consumers risk. Concepts of AQL, 
LTPD, AOQL in sampling, standard sample continuous and sequential 
sampling plans. 
9

POLYMER NANOCOMPOSITES 
Course Code 
PEPOT522 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Polymer Science 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
Study of fundamentals of Characterization and testing of polymers and polymer composites 
2. 
Understand the methodology for preparation of composite, various methods used for incorporation 
of nano fillers in polymers. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to composite material: - Introduction to polymer composites 
– Nano, micro and macro scales. Reinforcements – Short fibre, long fibre and 
particulate fillers. Matrices – thermoplastics-thermosets and rubbers, nano 
and micro composites. short and long fibre composites- Treatment of 
reinforcements. 
9  
2 
Polymer-filler interactions: -  use of coupling and bonding agents. 
Incorporation of reinforcements in polymer solution mixing- latex stage 
mixing-melt mixing and in-situ polymerization and precipitation – Dispersion 
and nucleating effects-Intercalation and exfoliation. 
9  
3 
Application of layered and nonlayered nano and micro particles in 
polymer modification: - Preparation of long fibre and short fibre composites 
Different methods of preparation of composites. Mechanism of film formation 
and drying, factors affecting coating properties, film thickness, film density, 
internal stresses, pigment volume concentration (PVC). different methods 
9 

 
 
used for film preparation, Mechanical and optical properties of coatings, 
ageing properties, effect of rheological behaviour on paint performance. 
4 
Adhesion properties of coatings: - factors affecting adhesive bond, 
thermodynamics of adhesion, testing of paint materials- destructive and non-
destructive methods, paint film defects, surface cleaning treatments, paint 
application methods.  
9

SEMESTER: S5 
CORROSION ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PEPOT523 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To impart knowledge on the importance of corrosion and its prevention and control in process 
industries.  
2. 
      To develop plans for fighting corrosion and develop anti corrosive systems. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Principles of corrosion phenomenon: Corrosion rate expressions, 
Electrochemical aspects, Environmental effects, Metallurgical and other 
aspects. 
9  
2 
Galvanic or two metal corrosion:  Crevice corrosion, Pitting, Intergranular 
corrosion, Selective leaching, Erosion corrosion, Stress corrosion, Hydrogen 
damage. 
9  
3 
Non-electrochemical and electrochemical methods: potentiostat, Tafel 
extrapolation, linear polarization, galvanostat, impedance spectroscopy, 
thermogravimetric technique, salt spray test, weight change measurements. 
9  
4 
Design and coatings:  inhibitors and surface engineering, cathodic protection 
and anodic protection.Corrosion and its control in industries: Power, Process, 
Petrochemical, ship building, marine and fertilizer industries. Corrosion 
auditing in industries, Corrosion map of India. 
9

SEMESTER: S5 
AIR POLLUTION CONTROL 
Course Code 
PEPOT524 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To make students aware of air pollution and methods for controlling different pollutants.  
2. Understanding the importance of measurement of air contents and quality control and the different 
methods employed for purification of air in industry and day to day life  
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction - Significance of air pollution studies, factors that contribute to 
air pollution - possibilities to air pollution abatemant - air pollution legislation 
- Techno - administrative aspects of air pollution - Emission and noise 
standards of Kerala State Pollution Control board. 
Gaseous pollutants-source, chemistry, adverse effects on plants, animals and 
human beings, properties - tolerance levels - carbon monoxide, carbon 
dioxide, aldehydes, hydrocarbons - compounds of sulphur, compounds of 
Nitrogen, Oxidants, Hydrogen fluoride - Control of gaseous pollutants - 
Automobile pollution control. 
9  
2 
Particulates in the air - source, nature and adverse effects - control of 
particulates - settling, filtration, collection in fluids, electrostatic precipitation, 
conversion to harmless and useful products. Meteorology related to 
atmosphere - pressure, temperature, lapse rates - humidity - condensation - 
9  

 
 
wind direction and velocity. Effects of meteorological parameters on transport 
and diffusion. Atmospheric electricity. 
3 
Optics of the atmosphere - Effects of air pollutants on atmospheric visibility 
- methods of measurement of visibility - Introduction to noise pollution. 
Photochemical reactions of the atmosphere. Purpose and principles of 
measurement of (1) High volume sampler (2) Exhaust gas analyser (petrol and 
diesel) (3) Stack sampler (4) Sound level meter - industrial hygiene and in 
plant safety to workers. 
9  
4 
Ventilation and Indoor Air Quality Control- An Overview of Indoor Air 
Quality, Basics of HVAC Systems; IAQ Issues and Impacts on Occupants; 
Application of Audits to Developing an IAQ Profile, Developing Management 
Plans, IAQ Problems; Control, Quantification and Measurement, Air Pollution 
Dispersion-Dispersion Theory Basics- Air Quality Impact of Stationary 
Sources- Models and Resources 
9

(L: T:P: R) 
3: 0:0: 0 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart basic knowledge on bioreactors. 
2. To impart knowledge on different modes of operation bioreactor. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Bioreactors - Function, description, working, advantages and 
limitations of stirred tank, airlift, airlift pressure cycle bioreactor, 
packed bed, fluidized bed, trickle bed and flocculated cell bioreactors. 
Novel Bioreactors-inverse fluid flow units, hollow fiber reactors, 
centrifugal field reactors, rotating drum bioreactor, spin filter 
bioreactor, disposable culture systems and wave bioreactor. 
9 
2 
Batch bioreactor, cell death in batch reactor, endogenous metabolism, 
maintenance, calculation of batch reaction time from ideal system for 
enzyme reaction and cell culture, batch reaction time with enzyme 
deactivation, calculation of total batchtime. Ideal continuous flow 
stirred tank bioreactor (CFSTBR)-chemostat, substrate conversion and 
biomass productivity, mean residence time 
9  

 
 
3 
comparison of batch bioreactor and single stage CFSTBR, wash out 
condition, stability of the chemostat, chemostat with cell recycle, 
comparison of steady-state biomass concentration and volumetric 
biomass productivity for a chemostat with and without cell recycle.: 
reactors, calculation Plug flow tubular reactor (PFTR), comparison of 
ideal mixed flow (batch and CFSTBR) and plug flow tubular of reactor 
length and residence time, recycling in PFTRs, analysis of recycle 
reactors. 
9  
4 
Design aspects of bioreactors, bioreactor geometry, guidelines for 
bioreactor design, bioreactor vessels, agitator assembly, mass transfer 
aspects, rheology and mixing, design, operation and types of agitators, 
power requirements for agitation, effects of agitation on mass transfer, 
oxygen delivery system - spargers, foam control system, factors 
affecting antifoam requirements, mass transfer between phases–factors 
affecting mass transfer between phases, oxygen uptake in fermenters 
9

SEMESTER: S5 
PROCESS MODELLING & SIMULATION 
Course Code 
PEPOT527 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Basic Knowledge of Heat 
Transfer, Mass Transfer, 
And Fluid Flow 
Operations.
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To understand the important physical phenomena from the problem statement. 
2. 
To develop model equations for the given system. 
3. 
To apply suitable numerical simulation methods for the solution of models. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Modelling and Fundamental Laws 
Definitions of Modelling, Uses of Mathematical Modelling, Classification of 
Modelling Techniques-Basic Modelling Principles. 
Fundamental Laws of Chemical Engineering: -Energy Equations-Continuity 
Equation-Equation of Motion - Transport Equations -Equations of State 
Equilibrium States -Chemical Kinetics 
9  
2 
Reactor Modelling: 
Models of Reactors-Mixing with Reaction-Reversible Reaction-Steam 
Jacketed Vessel-Isothermal Constant and Variable Holdup CSTR in Series 
9  
3 
Separation Process Modelling: 
Models of Separation Processes: - Multicomponent Flash Drum-Ideal Binary 
Distillation Column - Multicomponent Distillation Column, Batch 
Distillation-Condensation 
9  

 
 
4 
Distributed System Modelling and Numerical Simulation Techniques: 
Distributed System Modelling: Jacketed Tubular Reactor-Laminar Flow in a 
Pipe - Counter Current Liquid-Liquid Heat Exchanger 
Numerical Simulation Techniques: Finite Difference Method -Method of 
Weighted Residuals. Simulation of Gravity Flow Tank -CSTR in Series -Non-
Isothermal CSTR 
9

Link ID  
1 
Mathematical Modelling and Simulation of Chemical Engineering Processes by Prof. Sourav 
Mondal, IIT Kharagpur. 
This course covers mathematical modelling approaches, theoretical frameworks for heat, mass, 
and fluid flow, and includes simulation techniques 
(https://onlinecourses.nptel.ac.in/noc24_ch76/preview) 
(https://onlinecourses.nptel.ac.in/noc22_ch47/preview). 
2 
Chemical Process Control by Prof. S. Pushpavanam, IIT Madras. 
This course includes fundamental principles such as energy and continuity equations, equations 
of motion, transport equations, and equilibrium states 
3 
Chemical Reaction Engineering by Prof. Kannan Moudgalya, IIT Bombay. 
This course covers models of reactors, including mixing with reaction, reversible reactions, and 
steam jacketed vessels 
4 
Process Equipment Design by Prof. M. K. Jha, IIT Roorkee. 
This course includes models of separation processes like multicomponent flash drums and 
distillation columns 

 
 
SEMESTER: S5 
OIL AND NATURAL GAS ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PEPOT528 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. The field of natural gas engineering is very much important for petroleum engineers specializing 
in gas processing technology.  
2. The course outlines an optimal balance between natural gas production, natural gas processing and 
gas transportation. An extensive treatise on natural gas engineering, both upstream and gas refining 
processes with key equipment and facility design will be covered. 
3. This course will also highlight the current status of production of natural gas through 
unconventional sources/ techniques and the applications of natural gas. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of petroleum geology and exploration: Introduction, origin, 
formation, geological occurrence and characteristics of oil and natural gas. 
Source Rocks, Reservoir Rocks, and Cap rocks: Definition, Characteristics, 
Classification and nomenclature, Concept of Shale oil, Reservoir Properties, 
Hydrocarbon migration, Petroleum Exploration 
9  
2 
Conventional natural gas: Associated gas, non-associated gas, Gas 
condensate. Unconventional production of natural gas: Coal bed 
methane, Natural gas hydrate, shale gas and tight gas sands. 
Coal bed methane - Introduction, present status, formation and properties of 
coal bed methane. Natural Gas Hydrate - Concepts and Structures,  
9  

 
 
Estimation and Production of Natural Gas: Estimation of gas reserves 
by volumetric method – Production of natural gas –Pressure decline 
method  
3 
Dehydration of Natural gas: Water content of natural gas streams,hydrate 
control in gas production, dehydration systems - Glycol dehydration and Solid 
desiccant dehydration. 
Acid gas removal: Metaloxide process, Slurry process, Amine process, 
Carbonate washing process, Methanol based process and Sulphur recovery 
process. 
Compression of Natural Gas: Types of Compressors, Selection of 
reciprocating and centrifugal compressors, Thermodynamics of Compressors, 
Compression calculations. 
 
9  
4 
Gas flow measurement: Fundamentals, Methods of measurements, Orifice 
meters equation, turbine meters, Selection, Uncertainties in flow. 
Liquefied Natural Gas: Gas treating before liquefaction- Liquefaction 
cycles- Storage of LNG, Transportation-Regasification and cold utilization of 
LNG.  
Safety measures and environmental considerations. 
9

SEMESTER: S5 
POLYMER ELECTROLYTES & GELS 
Course Code 
PEPOT525 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course is designed to provide students the fundamental concepts of polymer gels and 
electrolytes 
2. To understand the preparation of polymer gels and polymer electrolytes as it is important to 
fabricate various products for various applications. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to polymer Electrolytes- Definition, composition, types of 
polymer electrolytes- solid polymer electrolytes, liquid polymer electrolytes, 
gel polymer electrolytes, ionic polymer electrolytes. Common polymers 
included as polymer electrolytes; different interactions seen in polymer 
electrolytes. Different synthesis method of polymer electrolytes, advantages 
and disadvantages of polymer electrolytes 
9  
2 
Properties & Applications of Polymer Electrolytes- ionic conductivity, ion-
transfer mechanism, chemical properties, mechanical & thermal properties, 
electro-chemical properties, electrochemical characterization by cyclic 
voltammetry and electrochemical impedance spectroscopy, optical properties, 
dielectric properties, solvation and desolvation kinetics, adhesion & cohesion, 
interfacial tension, contact angle.Applications in energy storage device, 
electrochemical sensors, optoelectronic devices and biomedical applications 
9  

 
 
3 
Polymer Gels: Polymer hydrogels, aerogels, macro, micro and nanogels, 
organogels. Cellulose based polymer gels, polysaccharide-based polymer 
gels, graphene oxide-based polymer gels, Functional polymer gels. 
Importance of crosslinking in gels. Examples of crosslinking agents. Various 
synthesis methods for polymeric gels. Factors influencing network formation 
in gels, different interactions in gels. 
9  
4 
Properties & Gelation- rheological properties, swelling study of gels, 
mechanical properties and its characterisation, role of gelation, factors 
influencing gelation. Biocompatibility of gels and its applications in various 
biomedical fields. Gels as shape memory materials, polymer gels for energy 
storage devices.  
9

(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks)

Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
 
1. 
Problem Definition (2 points) 
 
Check for clarity and completeness of the problem definition.  
 
Check for clear objectives and divide into sub objectives 
2. 
Problem Analysis (4 points) 
 
Examine the problem and identify the variables and responses 
 
Divide the problem to manageable parts 
3. 
Implementation of software (2 points) 
 
Use suitable software for getting the solution 
 
Check for the appropriateness of tools used 
4. 
Evaluate (4 points) 

 
 
 
Evaluate the proposed solution. 
 
Assess the correctness of solution. 
5. 
Validation of the results (4 points) 
 
Validate the results using available data. 
 
Do the error analysis of the results obtained. 
6. 
Conclusion and presentation (4 points) 
 
Summarize the results obtained  
 
Do critical thinking of the results obtained and evaluate. 
 
Submit a technical report

SEMESTER S5 
SPECIFICATION TEST LAB 
 
Course Objectives:  
1. 
To create practical knowledge on specification tests for latex and dry rubber 
2. 
To impart knowledge on properties of latex and dry rubber 
Details of Experiment 
Expt. No
Experiment 
1 
Specification tests for field latex Viscosity 
2 
Specification tests for field latex density 
3 
Specification tests for field latex pH 
4 
Specification tests for content of Ammonia preserved latex 
5 
Specification tests for Magnesium, Copper and manganese content of preserved latex 
6 
Specification tests for Dry rubber content, Total solid content, KOH number and Volatile 
fatty acid number of preserved latex                
7 
Specification tests for Sludge content and Coagulum content of preserved latex 
8 
Specification tests for Mechanical stability time, Heat stability time and ZnO stability of 
preserved latex 
9 
Specification tests for Volatile matter, Ash content and Dirt content of dry rubber 
10 
Specification tests for Nitrogen content of dry rubber 
11 
Specification tests for Estimation of Cu and Fe of dry rubber 
12 
Specification tests for Estimation of Mn, P0, PRI of dry rubber

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. 
Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
● 
Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test 
understanding of the upcoming experiment. 
● 
Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of 
the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. 
Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
● 
Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution of 
experiments, and following safety protocols. 
● 
Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
● 
Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
 
 
 
 

 
 
3. 
Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
● 
Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper 
documentation of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
● 
Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
● 
Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles 
during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, and 
record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. 
Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
● 
Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
● 
Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
● 
Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
● 
Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
2. 
Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
● 
Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or 
programming task. 
 
 

 
 
3. 
Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
● 
Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
● 
Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality 
of program output. 
4. 
Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
● 
Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
● 
Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the 
subject. 
5. 
Record (5 Marks) 
● 
Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

SEMESTER 6
 
POLYMER ENGINEERING

 
 
SEMESTER: S6 
POLYMER PRODUCTS - DESIGN & TESTING 
Course Code 
PCPOT601 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:1:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Plastic Materials, 
Rubber Technology
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide in depth knowledge about steps involved in polymer product design with the basic rules 
and formulations. 
2. Student will be able to design formulations of typical rubber products, its processing, and curing 
process. 
3. Students will be able to design plastic products with the specifications as per the testing standards. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No.
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Design fundamentals: Introduction, design principles, steps in product 
design, functional design, aesthetic design, effect of fillers on properties 
and performance. Long term property analysis, creep, stress relaxation, 
stress in products- tension, compression and shear, effect of cyclic loading, 
structural design of products under static and dynamic loads. 
11  
2 
Design features of products, inside and outside corners, wall thickness, 
ribs, tapers, draft angles, weld lines, gate size and location, tolerances, 
moulded-in-inserts, plastic threads, blind holes, undercuts, hinges, 
functional surfaces and lettering, snap fitting, welding 
11 
3 
Design principles of plastic products- gears, plastic bearings, piping, 
films, sheets, bottles, water tanks, wires and cables, Standard test methods 
of plastic products- pipe, film, sheet, PU foam, plastic optical goods, food 
packing containers. 
11  

 
 
4 
Design fundamentals: rubber product design features, compound design 
principles of natural Rubber, Styrene Butadiene Rubber, Butadiene Rubber, 
Acrylonitrile Butadiene Rubber, Chloroprene Rubber, Ethylene Propylene 
Diene Monomer, Isobutylene Isoprene Rubber.Testing of Rubber Products: 
Rubber bearings, bridge bearings, rubber seals, static and dynamic seals, 
hoses, couplings, beltings, cables, rubber to metal bonded products. 
11

SEMESTER: S6 
POLYMER TESTING 
Course Code 
PCPOT602 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Polymer Materials and 
Properties
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide in depth knowledge about focuses on the testing, analysis and characterization of 
polymeric materials. 
2. Student will be able to understand the international testing standards. 
3. Student will be able to perform testing of polymer products as per technically specified standards. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction – Need for testing, need for standards and specifications, national 
and international standards BIS, ASTM, BS, DIN, FDA etc. Specimen 
preparation and conditioning, standard for test specimen preparation like 
moulding, machining, stamping and punching of specimens, conditioning of 
specimen. 
9  
2 
Mechanical properties: a) Short term strengths: Tensile properties, compression 
properties, flexural properties, shear properties, impact resistance, toughness, 
Tear resistance, abrasion resistance and hardness. b) Long term strengths: 
Dynamic stress and strain properties and their measurements, creep, stress 
relaxation, fatigue properties, flexing, and resilience, heat build- up, ageing 
properties. 
9  

 
 
3 
Structural evaluation of polymers: Fourier transform infrared spectrometry, 
Ultraviolet - visible spectrometry, Nuclear magnetic resonance spectrometry, 
Mass spectrometry, X-ray diffraction spectrometry, Gas chromatography, 
Scanning Electron 
Microscopy, atomic force microscopy. Electrical properties: volume resistivity, 
surface resistivity, breaks down voltage, dielectric strength, dielectric constant, 
arc resistance, power factor. 
9  
4 
Thermal properties of polymers: Glass transition temperature, melting 
temperature, heat distortion temperature, etc.  Principle and uses of DTA, TGA, 
DSC and TMA. Optical properties: Gloss, haze, refractive index, transmittance. 
Other test: MFI, MVI, specific gravity, weathering properties, toxicity, resistance 
to chemicals, VST, HDT. 
9

PROJECT ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PEPOT631 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To Understand the Comprehensive Process of Project Development and Management. 
2. 
To Develop proficiency in Planning, Scheduling, and Execution Techniques. 
3. 
To Acquire Skills in Financial and Economic Evaluation. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Project Development and Engineering  
Classification of Projects, Scope of Project Engineering, Role of the Project 
Engineer 
Development of Projects: R&D, TEFR 
Importance of Laboratory Development: Bench Scale Experiments, Pilot 
Plant Studies, Semi-commercial Plant, Plant Location and Site Selection 
Preliminary Data for Construction Projects 
Process Engineering: Flow Diagrams, Plot Plans, Engineering Design and 
Drafting 
9  
2 
Project Planning, Scheduling, and Execution  
Planning and Scheduling of Projects: Bar Chart, PERT/CPM, Critical Path 
Calculations 
Site Development: Foundation, Erection, and Site Fabrication 
Construction: Alignment, Insulation 
Start-Up and Commissioning: Trial Runs, Guarantees, and Hand Over 
9  

 
 
Contracts and Contractors: Introduction, Detailing of Scope of Work, 
Factors in Selecting Scope of Work 
Contract Types: Detailing and Selection, Contractor Selection 
3 
Project Financing and Equipment Selection  
Selection of Process Equipment: Standard vs. Special Equipment, Selection 
Criteria, Specification Sheets 
Project Financing: Means of Finance, Financial Institutions, Special 
Schemes 
Financing in India: Financial Institutions, Key Financial Indicators, and 
Ratios 
Personnel Recruitment and Training 
Economic Evaluation of Projects: Capital Requirements, Cost of Production, 
Profitability, Break-Even Analysis, Minimum Cost Analysis 
9  
4 
Piping Engineering and Safety  
Scope of Piping Engineering, Pipe Sizing Technique, Codes and Standards 
in Piping Design 
Piping Design: Thermal Insulation and Buildings 
Safety in Plant Design 
9

SEMESTER S6 
POLYMERS & ENVIRONMENT 
Course Code 
PEPOT632 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
Impact of polymers on environment 
2. 
Remedial measures to reduce the harm caused by polymers 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Impact of polymers on environment:  
Introduction, resources of polymers, comparison of total energy costs for 
product manufacture based on polymers, ceramics and metals, polymer 
production and consumption, comparison of the impact of polymers and other 
materials on environment. 
Environmental pollution, non-biodegradability of polymers, drawbacks, 
burning of polymers, remedy for environmental problem by polymers, 
awareness program, need for recycling of plastics from urban solid wastes. 
 
9  
2 
Plastic waste segregation: 
Sorting and segregation of waste, plastics identification, SPI coding. Primary 
recycling, equipments for primary recycling, specific recycling techniques, PE 
films, PP battery case, crushing and separation, PET films, Secondary 
recycling, plastics wastes containing paper, hydrolytic treatment 
 
9  
3 
Rubber and mixed waste: 
Processing of mixed plastics waste, household waste, industrial sector, TPO 
based materials, use of recyclable plastics in motor vehicles, recoverable 
9  

 
 
material, disposal of residuals, recycling of rubber, difficulty in recycling of 
rubber products, reclaimator process, WTR, advantages of reclaimed rubber 
in cost, mixing and processing 
4 
Bio-degradation of polymers:  
 Introduction, enzymes, enzyme nomenclature, enzyme specificity, physical 
factors affecting the activity of enzymes, enzyme mechanism, chemical 
degradation initiates biodegradation, hydrolysis of synthetic biodegradable 
polymers. Development of starch-based polymers, manufacture of master 
batch, biodegradation, assessment, bio polyesters, synthesis, isolation, solvent 
extraction, properties, degradation, intracellular biodegradation, extra cellular 
biodegradation, thermal degradation, hydrolytic degradation, environmental 
degradation 
 
9

SEMESTER: S6 
CHEMICAL ENGINEERING THERMODYNAMICS 
Course Code 
PEPOT633 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Basic knowledge in 
Thermodynamics
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Students will grasp the fundamental principles and laws of thermodynamics. 
2. Students will become proficient in using P-V and P-T diagrams for pure substances, and equations 
of state for real gases 
3. To understand phase equilibria and chemical reaction equilibrium. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of Thermodynamics 
Thermodynamic Systems: closed, open, and isolated systems, Intensive and 
Extensive Properties, Path and State Functions, Reversible and Irreversible 
Processes 
Zeroth Law of Thermodynamics- First Law of Thermodynamics: Energy 
Balance for Closed Systems, Limitations of First Law- Second Law of 
Thermodynamics: Carnot’s Principles, Definition of Entropy, Calculation of 
Entropy Change in Processes Involving Ideal Gases 
Third Law of Thermodynamics, Energy Balance of Open Systems: Flow through 
Pipes, Nozzles, Compressors 
9  
2 
Thermodynamic Properties and Equations 
P-V and P-T Diagrams of Pure Substances 
9  

 
 
Equations of State for Real Gases: van der Waal’s, Redlich-Kwong, Peng-
Robinson, and Virial Equations, Principle of Corresponding States and 
Generalized Compressibility Chart, Fundamental Property Relations 
Maxwell’s Equations, Clausius-Clapeyron Equation 
Entropy-Heat Capacity Relationships: Equations for Entropy, Internal Energy, 
and Enthalpy in Terms of Measurable Quantities 
Joule-Thomson Coefficient, Gibbs-Helmholtz Equation 
Fugacity and Activity of Pure Fluids: Selection of Standard State, Effect of 
Temperature and Pressure 
3 
Solutions and Phase Equilibria 
Definition of Partial Molar Properties and Chemical Potential, Fugacity in 
Solution - Ideal Solution: Lewis-Randall Rule, Raoult’s Law, Henry’s Law, 
Activity in Solutions 
Activity Coefficient: Effect of Temperature and Pressure, Gibbs-Duhem 
Equations, Property Change of Mixing, Excess Properties 
Criterion of Phase Equilibria: Single Component and Multicomponent Systems, 
Criterion of Stability, Phase Rule for Non-reacting Systems, 
9 
4 
Vapor-Liquid Equilibria and Chemical Reaction Equilibria 
Vapor-Liquid Equilibrium (VLE): Phase Diagram for Binary Solutions 
VLE in Ideal and Non-Ideal Solutions: VLE at Low Pressures 
Activity Coefficient Models: Wohl’s Equation, Margules Equation, van Laar 
Equation, Wilson Equation (General Concepts Only) 
Equations of VLE at High Pressures, Definition of Vaporization Equilibrium 
Constant, Bubble Point, Dew Point, and Flash Calculations in Multicomponent 
Systems (Derivations Only) 
Chemical Reaction Equilibria: Extent of Reaction, Equilibrium Constant, 
Standard Free Energy Change, Feasibility of Reaction, Effect of Temperature on 
Equilibrium Constant, Evaluation of Equilibrium Constant 
9

SEMESTER: S6 
ADDITIVE MANUFACTURING 
Course Code 
PEPOT634 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To educate students with fundamental and advanced knowledge in the field of additive 
manufacturing technology 
SYLLABUS 
Module No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction and basic principles: Need for Additive Manufacturing, 
Generic AM process, the benefits of AM, distinction between AM and 
CNC machining, classification of AM processes, metals systems, hybrid 
systems, the eight steps in additive manufacture, variations from one AM 
machine to another, materials handling issues, design for AM, and 
application areas. 
9   
2 
Photo polymerization processes: Stereo lithography (SL), Materials, SL 
resin curing process, Benefits and Drawbacks, Applications of Photo 
polymerization Processes. Powder bed fusion processes: Selective laser 
Sintering (SLS), Materials, Powder fusion mechanism, SLS Metal and 
ceramic part creation, Electron Beam melting (EBM), Process Benefits 
and Drawbacks, Applications of Powder Bed Fusion Processes. 
Extrusion-based systems Fused Deposition Modelling (FDM), Principles, 
Materials, Bio-Extrusion, Process Benefits and Drawbacks, Applications 
of Extrusion-Based Processes.Sheet Lamination AM Processes: Bonding 
9  

 
 
Mechanisms, Materials, Laminated Object Manufacturing (LOM), 
Ultrasonic Consolidation (UC), Gluing, Thermal bonding, LOM and UC 
applications. 
3 
Additive manufacturing systems: Powder Bed Fusion AM Processes: 
Selective laser Sintering (SLS), Materials, Powder fusion mechanism and 
powder handling, SLS Metal and ceramic part creation, Electron Beam 
melting (EBM), Process Benefits and Drawbacks, Applications of 
Powder Bed Fusion Processes. Directed Energy Deposition AM 
Processes: Process Description, Material Delivery, Laser Engineered Net 
Shaping (LENS), Direct Metal Deposition (DMD), Electron Beam Based 
Metal Deposition, Benefits and drawbacks, Applications of Directed 
Energy Deposition Processes. Materials science for AM - Multifunctional 
and graded materials in AM, Role of solidification rate, microstructural 
studies, Structure property relationship, Three-Dimensional Printing– 
Principle, process, advantages and applications- 
9  
4 
Choosing materials for manufacturing: Multiple materials, metal AM 
processes, Composite Materials, Biomaterials, Hierarchical Materials, 
Ceramics & Bio-ceramics, Shape-Memory Materials, 4D Printing, 
Advanced AM Materials. Medical and bio additive manufacturing, 
Customized implants and prosthesis: Design and production, Bio-
Additive Manufacturing- Computer Aided Tissue Engineering (CATE), 
Case studies 
9

Course Code

CIE Marks

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To provide in depth knowledge from methodology of impact analysis, socio impact analysis, air 
quality impact analysis and water quality impact analysis. 
2. Understand the fundamentals of environmental impact and factors for consideration in assessing 
environmental impact analysis. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Concepts of environmental impact analysis-Environmental protections, 
legislations, laws and Acts-air quality legislation-energy legislation-fish and 
wild life resources.  
9  
2

assessing environmental impact concept short term vs. long term effects. Socio 
impact analysis-physical, social, aesthetic and economic environment- 
examples of types of socio impact analysis.

3

analysis-effects of noise on people-estimating transportation noise impact-
examples.

4

modelling-water quality impact by projects like High ways, power plants, 
agriculture and irrigation, forest management, vegetation and wild life impact 
analysis. Assessment methodologies- impact on biota-summarisation of 
environmental impact-checklist method.

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart knowledge of processes like cracking, reforming, alkylation, coking and asphalt 
technology. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Origin of Petroleum: - Origin- exploration and production of petroleum, 
testing of petroleum products, types of crudes, composition, characteristics, 
product pattern, crude heating, distillation principles, stripping, atmospheric 
and vacuum distillation, heat balance and material balance in distillation, types 
of trays, quality control 
9  
2 
Refining processes: - Cracking, Thermal Cracking and Vis breaking, Hydro 
Cracking- principles, reactions in Hydro Cracking, Catalyst, Hydro Cracking 
reaction Conditions. Different Feed Stocks, Products Yields, Qualities and 
Recent Development. Catalytic Cracking, Commercial Catalyst, Feedstock 
and Catalytic Cracking Conditions, Types and Processes- Fixed Bed Cracker, 
Fluid Catalytic Cracking (FCC), Flexi Cracking. 
9  
3 
Catalytic reforming &cocking: - Theory, Reaction Conditions and Catalyst 
for Catalytic Reforming, Platforming, Hurdy Forming, Rheine Forming, 
Power Forming, Selector Forming. Ultra-Forming and Rex Forming., 
9 

 
 
Feedstock Selection and Effect of Steam. Coking Methods of Petroleum, Coke 
Production, Delayed Coking, Fluid Coking and Contact Coking. 
4 
Asphalt technology: - Source of Asphalt (Bitumen), Chemical Structure of 
Asphalt, Action of Heat on Asphalt, Types of Asphalts. Air Blowing of 
Bitumen and Upgradation of Heavy Crudes. Specialty Products: Industrial 
Grease- Manufacture of Calcium Grease, Liquid Paraffin and Petroleum 
Jellys. 
9

SEMESTER: S6 
ADVANCED NANOCOMPOSITES 
Course Code 
PEPOT635 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Basic Knowledge in 
Polymer Science
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
Aims to impart knowledge on advanced nanocomposite materials. 
2. 
To gain ability to design nanocomposites based on the need and specifications. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Nanocomposites & Nanofillers: Overview of polymer nanocomposites; 
Classification of nanofillers: Nano clay, nano silica, nanoparticles, carbon 
based nanofillers; Synthesis and properties of fillers. Synthesis of 
Nanocomposites: Direct mixing, solution mixing, in-situ polymerization, ex-
situ 
processing; 
Ceramic/polymer 
composites; 
Metal/polymer 
nanocomposites; Modification of interfaces; Modification of nanofillers. 
9   
2 
Particulate polymer composites  
Particulate polymer composites: Characteristics for a particulate reinforcer, its 
selection and its surface coatings, mineral, metallic and organic particulate 
reinforcers, processing of particulate polymer composite and product 
development, mechanics, models and equations for Young’s Modulus of the 
composites, applications of particulate composites  
9   
3 
FRP Composites 
Synthetic FRP composites, natural FRP composites; Short fiber composites; 
processing of short FRP composite, product development and manufacturing, 
collimated fiber compounds, fiber length distribution on the composites, short 
9   

 
 
natural FRP composites, processes and manufacturing, applications, hybrid 
composites, Mechanical properties of short FRP composites. Continues FRP 
composites; Natural, inorganic and synthetic continuous FRP composites, 
processing and manufacturing of thermoset FRP composites by Vacuum Bag 
Molding, Vacuum infusion Molding, Resin Transfer Molding, Pultrusion and 
Filament Winding, structural and other applications of thermoset composites. 
Limitations of Processing and manufacturing, Mechanical and thermal 
properties of continues FRP composites, Applications 
4 
Properties, Characterisation & Applications – Thermal, electrical & optical 
properties, mechanical properties, morphological & barrier properties. 
Applications of polymer nanocomposites in space, automobiles, defence, 
electronics, packaging, bio-medical engineering, filtration, coatings and 
cosmetic. Microstructure evaluation by scanning electron and optical 
microscopes. Structure evaluation by FTIR, NMR, C-13 NMR, UV. Elemental 
analysis – qualitative and quantitative, Dielectric measurements, Diffusion 
properties, Thermo-mechanical properties, DMA creep, thermal relaxations., 
contact angle measurements.  
9

1.

2.

 
Divide the problem to manageable parts 

 
 
3.

 
Use suitable software for getting the solution 


4. 
Evaluate (4 points) 
 
Evaluate the proposed solution. 
 
Assess the correctness of solution. 
5. 
Validation of the results (4 points) 


 
Do the error analysis of the results obtained. 
6.

Summarize the results obtained

 
Submit a technical report

Suggestion on Project Topics 
1. 
After completion of first module students are able to prepare blend by any one of the   methods 
2. 
After completion of second module students are able to collect the datas of miscible and immiscible 
blend and familiarize different types of fibres used in composites. 
3. 
After completion of third module students are able to produce polymer concrete.  
4. 
 After completion of fourth module students are able to prepare one FRP product by hand lay-up 
process.

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. 
Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
●

understanding of the upcoming experiment. 
● 
Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and understanding of 
the theoretical background related to the experiments.

experiments, and following safety protocols. 
● 
Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in observations, and 
troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
● 
Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 
3. 
Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
● 
Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper 
documentation of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
● 
Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough record and 
maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
4. 
Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
● 
Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying principles 
during a viva voce session. 

 
 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, viva, and 
record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. 
Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
● 
Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure and 
understanding each step involved. 
● 
Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
● 
Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related to the 
experiment. 
● 
Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
● 
Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment or 
programming task. 
3. 
Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
● 
Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
● 
Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment or quality 
of program output. 
4. 
Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
● 
Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related questions 
● 
Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects of the 
subject. 
5. 
Record (5 Marks) 
● 
Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

Course Code

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Develop knowledge on manufacturing, testing and applications of fibres 
2. Impart knowledge on various kinds of fibres. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction, definition of fibre, fibre dimensions, units of measurements, 
tex,denier, conversion from one system to another, use of fibres in the rubber and 
plastic industry, polymer products containing fibres, fibre manufacturing 
industries in India, present status and future prospects Fibres used in polymer 
industry-types and sources, chemical composition, properties, concept of order in 
fibres and polymers, crystallinity and orientation, orientation and fibre properties 
9  
2 
Methods of investigating fibre structure. use of animal and mineral fibres. Detailed 
study of fibre properties such as mechanical properties, electrical properties, 
moisture absorption, moisture regain optical properties and fibre friction, relation 
between fibre properties and structure, uses of vegetable fibres such as cotton, flax, 
linen, coir, sisal, pineapple, jute, silk, banana 
9  
3 
Manmade fibres, physical structure of fibre forming polymers, production, 
chemical composition, properties and testing of viscose rayon, cellulose acetate, 
9  

 
 
nylon66 and nylon6, polyester, acrylic, poly vinyl alcohol, spandex, carbon fibre, 
metallic fibres, saran, Kevlar, Nomex, steel wire, finishing and dyeing. 
4 
Yarn and textile production from fibres, definition of various textile terms, fibre 
spinning, drawing of fibres, felting, knitting, lacing, bonding and weaving, 
properties of yarns, yarn numbering system, brief idea about spinning of cotton 
yarns and blends .Yarn properties such as count appearance, evenness, strength, 
abrasion, fatigue, friction, twist, dynamic mechanical properties and their 
importance, fabrics, brief idea about the construction, cover factor, geometry of 
weaves, fabric properties such as strength, abrasion resistance, air permeability, 
bursting strength, thermal properties 
9

SEMESTER: S7 
COMPUTER AIDED DESIGN & MANUFACTURE 
Course Code 
PEPOT 742 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
Understand the Foundations of CAD Systems. 
2. 
Develop Skills in Geometric Modeling and Transformations. 
3. 
Master Computerized Manufacturing and CNC Programming. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to CAD (Computer aided design): 
CAD system architecture- Packages for CAD/CAM/CAE/CAPP. Hardware in 
CAD components, user interaction devices, design database, graphic 
Standards, data Exchange Formats 
Geometric transformations: 
Transformation of points and line, 2-D rotation, reflection, scaling and 
combined transformation, homogeneous coordinates, 3-D scaling. Shearing, 
rotation, reflection and translation, combined transformations. Algebraic and 
geometric forms, tangents and normal, blending functions, re-parametrization, 
straight lines, conics, cubic splines, Bezier curves and B-spline curves. 
9  
2 
Geometric Modeling: 
Plane surface, ruled surface, surface of revolution, tabulated cylinder, bi cubic 
surface, Bezier surface, B-spline surfaces and their modelling techniques. 
9  

 
 
Solid models and representation scheme, boundary representation, 
constructive solid geometry. Sweep representation, cell decomposition, spatial 
occupancy enumeration, coordinate systems for solid modelling. 
3 
Computerized Manufacture Planning and Control System: 
Computer Aided Process Planning, benefits of CAPP, Production Planning 
and Control Systems, typical activities of PPC System, computer integrated 
production management system, Material Requirement Planning, inputs to 
MRP system, working of MRP, outputs and benefits. 
Flexible Manufacturing Systems: 
Fundamentals of Group Technology and Flexible Manufacturing Systems, 
types of FMS, FMS components, Material handling and storage system, 
applications, benefits, computer control systems, Automated Storage and 
Retrieval Systems, AS/RS and Automatic parts identification systems and data 
capture. 
9  
4 
Computer Numerical Control: 
Introduction, components of CNC, CNC programming, manual part 
programming, G Codes, M Codes, programming of simple components in 
turning, drilling and milling systems, programming with canned cycles. Cutter 
radius compensations. 
Robot Technology: 
Robot anatomy, joints and links, common robot configurations, robot control 
systems, accuracy and repeatability, end effectors, sensors in robotics. Robot 
programming methods: on-line and offline methods. Robot industrial 
applications: material handling, processing and assembly and inspection. 
9

SEMESTER: S7 
POLYMERS & FUEL CELL TECHNOLOGY 
Course Code 
PEPOT743 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Engineering Chemistry, 
Polymer Materials. 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Study of fundamentals of developments made in fuel cell development and the challenges 
facing in its wide practical applications.  
2. Understand the methodology for research on future prospects in the development and 
applications of fuel cell.   
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fuel Cell, Brief History of fuel cells, Fuel Cell and conventional processes – 
comparison, Types of Fuel Cells Application scenarios, Advantages and 
disadvantages, Energy & power relations, units, Working of a PEM fuel Cell, 
Polymer materials as components of fuel cell, Major Cell Components, 
Material Properties, Processes and Operating Conditions of PEMFC. 
9  
2 
Gibb's free energy -Work potential of fuel, Reversible voltage, NERNST 
Equation, Voltage and P, T and concentration dependence examples, 
Faraday's Laws, Efficiency: thermodynamic, voltage and fuel. 
Electrochemical reaction fundamentals, electrode kinetics, Charge transfer 
and activations energy, Exchange current density - slow and fast reactions, 
Potential and equilibrium - galvanic potential, Reaction rate and potential - 
Butler Volmer equation & Tafel equation, Exchange Currents and 
9  

 
 
Electrocatalysis: How to Improve Kinetic Performance, Electrode design 
basics. 
3 
Charge transport resistances, voltage losses, Ionic and electronic 
conductivities, Ionic conduction in different FC electrolytes: Aqueous, 
polymeric and ceramic, Diffusive transport & voltage loss: Limiting current 
density, Nernstian and kinetic effect, Convective transport: flow channels, gas 
diffusion / porous layer, gas velocity, pressure. 
9  
4 
Sizing of a Fuel Cell Stack, Stack Configuration, Uniform distribution of 
Reactants, Heat removal, Stack Clamping. 
Fuel Cell Diagnostics: Polarization Curve, Current Interrupt, AC Impedance 
Spectroscopy, Pressure drop as a diagnostic tool.Fuel Cell System Design: 
Hydrogen-Oxygen Systems, Hydrogen-Air Systems, Fuel Cell Systems with 
Fuel Processor, System Efficiency 
Fuel Cells and Hydrogen Economy: Hydrogen Energy Systems, Hydrogen 
Energy Technologies, Transition to Hydrogen Economy. 
9

SEMESTER: S7 
COMPOSITE MATERIALS 
Course Code 
PEPOT744 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1.  Impart the basic concepts of composite materials.  
 2. Develop knowledge on Composite behaviour and application. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
General characteristics of composites, advantages and disadvantages, 
advantages of using composites in high performance structures application 
trends. Composite applications in aircraft, space, transportation, energy 
electronics, sports and medical industries. Characteristics of fibres, matrices, 
interface bonding, adhesives microstructure of composites, the function of the 
fibre and matrix in a composite. Thermoplastic and thermoset matrix 
composites. Composite products and their unique properties. The 
strengthening mechanism that makes composites stronger. Environmental 
effects to design of composite structures. 
9 
2 
Traditional and novel approaches process fundamentals. Fundamental physics 
in composite manufacturing, manufacturing processes for polymeric 
composites. Typical defects introduced in manufacturing and the methods 
utilized to minimize these defects. Common terminology in composites 
manufacturing. Special tooling considerations required for composite 
manufacturing Basic concepts, stiffness, strength, thermal and moisture 
9 

 
 
expansion. Anisotropic and isotropic materials, tailored specific strengths. The 
cause of discontinuous stresses in composites and how it differs from metals 
3 
Laminate theory; micromechanical behaviour of a ply, out-of-plane effects. 
Hooke’s Law to unidirectional composites. The stress-strain relations of a 
unidirectional composite subjected to mechanical, thermal and moisture loads. 
Stress/strain/curvature of a laminate under constant axial forces and bending 
moments. The unusual behaviours which may occur in laminates such as 
bending/stretching coupling and stretching-shear coupling. The use of a 
specific layup orientation based on the loading conditions and CLT. The role 
of lamina and their arrangement in laminate Failure criteria, Laminate 
Strength, Stress Concentrations. 
9 
4 
The service life (fatigue) and environmental (damage/corrosion) effects on 
metallic vs. composite structures. Key damage mode for composites and 
composite damage tolerance capabilities How do actual composites for 
aerospace, automotive, sporting goods, high temperature applications behave? 
Problem areas, long-term performance, influence of structural geometries the 
Advantages and disadvantages of composites with respect to Product 
Lifecycle Management. General considerations and process involved in 
composite structural design. Typical in-service damage types for composites. 
Non-destructive inspection techniques for detecting damage in composites. 
Basic types of composite repair and their benefits 
9

Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Students should achieve sufficient knowledge about the basics of polymers for space 
application. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Polymers for aerospace research- adhesives, coatings, ablatives. Synthesis 
and processing of advanced thermoplastics: PEEK, polycarbonates, 
polyethers, polyether sulphones. Synthesis and processing of thermal 
protection systems in space research. High temperature resistant resins such 
as epoxy, phenolic and polyimides 
9  
2 
High temperature resistant polymers with metals in their back bone - 
Boron, Silicon and Phosphorous contain polymers for space applications, 
composites for satellites and launch vehicles: Composites- type of composites- 
fibre composites, particulate composites, foam composites. Desired properties 
of a matrix. Polymer matrix: Thermosets and thermoplastics. Fibre reinforced 
polymer (FRP) Types of fibres, mechanical properties of fibres, glass fibres, 
carbon fibres, aramid fibres, metal fibres, alumina fibres, boron fibres, silicon 
carbide fibres, silica fibres, etc 
9  

 
 
3 
Role of reinforcement: Theory of reinforcement property dependence on 
resin and reinforcement, directional properties. Laminated composites- 
Lamina & Laminate lay-up, ply-orientation definition. Strength of laminates, 
laminate stiffness and ABD Matrices, special classification of laminates, 
symmetric, antisymmetric and non-symmetric laminates.  
Failure mechanics of composites. Propellant binders, classification of 
propellants- solid, liquid, hybrid and air breathing. Solid propellants – 
homogenous smokeless propellants, Heterogeneous (composite) propellants. 
High energy binders- synthesis, characteristics, applications. Glycidylazide 
polymer and its homologues, polynitrato methyl methyloxetane, poly glycidyl 
nitrates. 
9  
4 
Testing of Composites: Mechanical testing of composites, tensile testing, 
compressive testing, intra laminar shear testing, inter laminar shear testing, 
fracture testing etc. Joining of composites: Adhesively bonded joints & 
mechanically fastened joints, environmental effects on composites. Composite 
characterization by mechanical, thermal and DMTA techniques.  
9

SEMESTER: S7 
LIQUID CRYSTAL POLYMERS 
Course Code 
PEPOT747 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Basic Understanding 
of Polymer Science 
and Engineering, 
Including Polymer 
Chemistry, Properties, 
And Processing. 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To achieve sufficient knowledge about the basics of liquid crystal polymers 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
INTRODUCTION- crystals, liquids, liquid crystals, polymers, history of 
liquid crystal polymers, structural requirements of LCP, types of liquid 
crystalline (LC) phases, MLC, PLC. 
9  
2 
TYPES OF LIQUID CRYSTALLINE POLYMERS- main chain and 
sidechain LC polymers, dendrimers, anisotropic properties, nematic, 
cholesterics, smectic, mesophase lyotropic, thermotropic, calamitic, discotic, 
structural features of side chain LC polymers, spacer length, mesogenic groups 
9  
3 
THEORIES OF LIQUID CRYSTALLINITY IN POLYMERS-, steric 
theory, Onsager approach, Flory’s lattice model, Advantages of LCP, 
disadvantages of LCP, Effect of electric and magnetic field, surface effect, 
birefringence in LCLC block copolymers, polymer dispersed LC, LC blends 
9  

 
 
composites, LC elastomers, LC ionomers. Characterization of LC phases, 
DSC, POM, XRD, NMR, FTIR, dielectric studies 
4 
APPLICATIONS OF LC POLYMERS- photochromic LC polymers, photo 
responsive LC polymers as sensors, LCD devices, high strength fibers, 
inorganic LC polymers, photomechanical LC actuators 
9

SEMESTER: S7 
PLASTICS PACKAGING TECHNOLOGY 
Course Code 
PEPOT748 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Plastic materials, 
Processing 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Study of fundamentals of plastic materials, its properties, processing techniques and 
applications for packaging applications.  
2. Understand the methodology for selection of packaging equipments, packaging equipment 
checklist, wrapping, sealing methods 
 
SYLLABUS 
 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to plastics packaging, functions of packaging, advantages of 
plastic packaging, distribution hazards, special requirements of food and 
medical packaging, packaging legislation and regulation, packaging as a 
system, elements, approach, package, design, relation criteria for packaging 
materials, packaging equipment checklist, case histories. 
9  
2 
Major packaging plastics, introduction, PE, PP, PS, PVC, polyesters, PVDC, 
vinylacetate, PVA, EVA, PV Alcohol, PA, PC ionomers & fluoro polymers. 
Conversion process, compression & transfer moulding, injection moulding. 
 
 
9  

 
 
3 
Blow moulding, extrusion, rotary thermoforming, lamination, metallizing, 
decoration process, shrink wrapping, pallet & stretch wrapping, sealing 
methods, plasma barrier coatings, energy requirement for conversion, 
extrusion, film and flexible packaging, extrusion, cast film & sheet, blown 
film, multi-layer film & sheet coatings, laminations & co extrusions, stretch 
and shrink wrap, pouching, sealing, evaluation of seals in flexible packages, 
advantages of flexible packaging, flexible packaging products, specialized 
packaging for food products. 
9  
4 
Thermoformed, moulded and rigid packages, thermoforming packages, 
position & thermoforming & wrap forming, solid phase pressure forming,skin 
packaging, thermoforming moulds, advantages & disadvantages of moulding 
foams, other cushioning materials & distribution packaging, polystyrene & 
other foams systems cushioning, design of moulded cushioning systems, 
plastic pallets, drums & other shipping containers, testing plastic packages, 
barrier, printing, labelling& pigmenting, sterilization systems and health care 
products, packaging hazards and their controls, environmental considerations. 
9

SEMESTER: S7 
POLYMER REACTION ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PEPOT745 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Basic Knowledge in 
Polymer Science 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart knowledge of application of reaction engineering for polymer production 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction To Reactor Design: Design equation for single reaction 
system, parallel and series reactions, temperature dependant terms, 
interpretation of batch reactor data, conversion, concentration and mole 
balance, constant volume reaction system, rate of reaction, first and zero order 
reaction 
9  
2 
Reaction Engineering of Free Radical Polymerisation: thermodynamics 
and kinetic aspects of free radical polymerisation MWD of 
free radical polymerisation: Standard free radical polymerisation; 
design of tubular reactors involving radical polymerisation, 
solution of equations describing isothermal radical polymerisation 
Reaction Engineering of Ionic, Ziggler Natta: Smith-Ewart and other 
models, average chain length estimation of stereoregular polymers, chain 
segment estimation and its distribution, classification of various ionic species, 
effect of solvent, ionophores and ionogens 
9  
3 
Reaction Engineering of Step Growth Polymerisation: kinetics of step 
growth polymerisation, accessibility of functional groups, equilibrium 
9  

 
 
considerations: closed and open systems, cyclisation versus linear 
polymerisation, MWD in linear and non-linear polymerisations 
4 
Bulk, Solution and Precipitation Polymerisations: Modelling of 
bulk and solution polymerisation reactor, precipitation 
polymerization: reactor modelling to interpret MWD of industrial 
polymers. Suspension and Emulsion Polymerisation: Suspension 
Polymerization: Principles, of reactor modelling and MWD estimation; 
Modelling of emulsion reactors, prediction of MWD and solution viscosity, 
examples 
9  
 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE): 
 
Attendance 
Internal Ex 
Evaluate 
Analyse 
Total 
5 
15 
10 
10 
40 
 
Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
1. 
Problem Definition (2 points) 
● 
Check for clarity and completeness of the problem definition.  
● 
Check for clear objectives and divide into sub objectives 
2. 
Problem Analysis (4 points) 
● 
Examine the problem and identify the variables and responses 
● 
Divide the problem to manageable parts 
3. 
Implementation of software (2 points) 
● 
Use suitable software for getting the solution 
● 
Check for the appropriateness of tools used 
 
 
 

 
 
4. 
Evaluate (4 points) 
● 
Evaluate the proposed solution. 
● 
Assess the correctness of solution. 
5. 
Validation of the results (4 points) 
● 
Validate the results using available data. 
● 
Do the error analysis of the results obtained. 
6. 
Conclusion and presentation (4 points) 
● 
Summarize the results obtained  
● 
Do critical thinking of the results obtained and evaluate. 
● 
Submit a technical report

SEMESTER: S7 
SPECIALITY POLYMERS 
Course Code 
PEPOT751 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Basic Understanding 
of Polymer Science 
and Engineering, 
Including Polymer 
Chemistry, Properties, 
And Processing. 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To learn about the design, synthesis, and structure-property relation of high 
performance and specialty polymers. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
High Temperature and Fire-Resistant Polymers– fluoropolymers, 
aromatic polymers, hydrocarbon polymers, polyphenylene sulphide, 
polysulphones, polyesters, aromatic polyamides, polyketones, heterocyclic 
polymers, fire resistant polymers, flame retardants.  
9  
2 
Ionic Polymers– Synthesis and physical properties: Ion-exchange, 
hydrophilicity, applications, ionomers based on polyethylene, elastomeric 
ionomers, ionomers based on polystyrene, PTFE, ionomers with 
polyaromatic backbones. Polyelectrolytes: ion exchangers, polyelectrolytes 
based on carboxylates, polyelectrolyte complexes.  
9  
3 
Polymers With Novel Properties– Liquid crystalline polymers (LCPs): 
concept of liquid crystalline (LC) phase, liquid crystalline polymers and their 
classification, main chain LCPs and side chain LCPs, structure-property 
9  

 
 
relationship, applications of LCPs. Conducting polymers: charge carriers, 
doping, synthesis of polyacetylene, polyaniline, polypyrrole, polythiophene. 
Photo conducting polymers.   
4 
Inorganic Polymers- polymers containing phosphorous, nitrogen and boron, 
organometallic polymers, polysiloxanes. Polymers for special applications – 
Polymer concretes, polymer binders for propellants, polymer-bonded 
explosives. Polymeric materials used in telecommunication and power 
transmission. Polymers in agricultural applications: green houses, mulches 
9

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart the basic concepts of separation process. 
2. Develop knowledge on recent advances in separation techniques 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Characteristics and selection of separation process: Importance and variety of 
separation, economic significance, inherent separation factor, selection, factors 
influencing the choice of separation process, solvent selection, selection of 
equipment. Recent advances in separation techniques based on size, surface 
properties, ionic properties and other special characteristics of substances, Rate 
based versus equilibrium separation processes, Selection of separation process, 
Energy requirements of separation processes. Polymer materials used as 
membranes, functional polymer membranes 
9  
2 
Introduction, Type and choice of membranes, Plate and frame, tubular, spiral 
wound and hollow fibre membrane reactors and their relative merits, 
Membrane filtration, Microfiltration, Nanofiltration, Ultrafiltration, Reverse 
Osmosis, Dialysis, Models for membrane separations. 
9  

 
 
Basic principles, classifications, Surfactants at Inter phases and in bulk, Foam 
fractionation, Foam flotation, Adsorptive bubble separations, Ion flotation, 
Microemulsion/Macro emulsions, Hydro topes, Solvent ablation 
3 
Interacting solutes, Adiabatic adsorbers, velocity effects. Adsorption- 
Desorption operations: Thermal desorption of gases, activated carbon solute 
recovery, processing liquid using thermal regeneration, Pressure swing and 
vacuum swing adsorption, Regeneration with purge and desorbent. Basics of 
Ionex change, Ionex change resins, Binary ion exchange equilibrium, Ion 
movement theory, Applications, Applications without exchange: Ion 
exclusion, Mass transfer in ion exchange systems 
9  
4 
Introduction, types of chromatography, Elution chromatography: Principles 
and Retention theory, Band broadening and separation efficiency, Types of 
chromatography, large scale elution (cyclic/batch) chromatography, Selective 
adsorption of biological macromolecules, Simulated counter current 
techniques, Comparison with other separation methods. 
9

SEMESTER: S7 
MODERN METHODS OF INSTRUMENTATION 
Course Code 
PEPOT 753 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Understand the principles and applications of modern instrumentation methods in 
polymer engineering. 
2. Gain knowledge about different characterization and testing techniques specific to 
polymers. 
3. Learn advanced measurement techniques and data acquisition methods. 
4. Explore emerging technologies and their applications in polymer instrumentation. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of Instrumentation in Polymer Engineering 
Introduction to Instrumentation in Polymer Engineering: Importance 
and applications of instrumentation in polymer engineering. Overview 
of traditional vs. modern instrumentation methods. Measurement 
Systems: Elements of a measurement system. Static and dynamic 
characteristics of instruments. Sensors and Transducers Specific to 
Polymers: Principles of sensors and transducers. Types of sensors: 
temperature, pressure, strain, and humidity sensors used in polymer 
processing. Signal Conditioning and Data Acquisition: Amplifiers, 
filters, and converters. Analog to Digital and Digital to Analog 
9  

 
 
Conversion (ADC/DAC). Components of Data Acquisition Systems 
(DAS) and their applications in polymer engineering.  
2 
Characterization Techniques for Polymers 
Thermal 
Analysis: 
Differential 
Scanning 
Calorimetry 
(DSC). 
Thermogravimetric Analysis (TGA). Dynamic Mechanical Analysis (DMA). 
Spectroscopic Methods: Fourier Transform Infrared Spectroscopy (FTIR). 
Nuclear Magnetic Resonance (NMR) Spectroscopy. Raman Spectroscopy. 
Chromatographic Techniques: Gel Permeation Chromatography (GPC). High-
Performance Liquid Chromatography (HPLC). Microscopy and Imaging: 
Scanning Electron Microscopy (SEM). Transmission electron microscopy 
(TEM). Atomic Force Microscopy (AFM). 
9  
3 
Advanced Instrumentation in Polymer Processing and Testing 
Process Instrumentation: Instrumentation for extrusion, injection molding, and 
blow molding. Real-time monitoring and control in polymer processing. 
Mechanical Testing of Polymers: Tensile, compressive, and flexural testing. 
Impact and hardness testing. Rheological Measurements: Principles of 
rheology and viscoelastic measurements. Rheometers and their applications in 
polymer engineering. Surface and Interface Characterization: Contact angle 
measurements. Surface energy analysis. Atomic Force Microscopy (AFM) for 
surface characterization. 
9  
4 
Emerging Technologies and Applications in Polymer Instrumentation 
Smart Sensors and IoT in Polymer Engineering: Integration of IoT in polymer 
instrumentation. Smart sensors and real-time data analytics. Polymer 
Nanocomposites and Instrumentation: Characterization techniques for 
nanocomposites. Challenges and solutions in nano composite instrumentation. 
Biomedical Applications of Polymers: Instrumentation in the development of 
polymer-based biomedical devices Characterization of biocompatible 
polymers. Sustainability and Environmental Monitoring: Instrumentation for 
recycling and degradation of polymers. Monitoring environmental impact of 
polymer materials. 
9

SEMESTER: S7 
 SAFETY ENGINEERING OF PROCESS PLANTS 
Course Code 
PEPOT754 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objective:  
1. 
This course introduces students to the concepts of process safety, safety practices in 
industries and emergency procedures.  
2. 
It also outlines the various types of hazards and risk. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Concept and importance of process safety. Safety in the site selection 
and layout. Review of Industrial Accidents-Major Chemical Industry 
Accidents, Bhopal, Flix borough, SEVESO. Cost of accidents. Material 
safety data sheet (MSDS). Work permit system, Personal Protective 
Equipments (PPE). 
Regulatory Bodies: -National safety council, OSHA, Loss prevention 
association, PESO, NEBOSH. 
9  
2 
Chemical Hazards: - Fire triangle, LFL, UFL, Types of fire- Pool fire, 
jet fire, Flash fire and Fire ball. Fire prevention techniques in process 
industry. Flammability diagram-construction and application. 
Explosion: - Deflagration, Detonation, UVCE, BLEVE and Dust explosion. 
Prevention techniques for explosion 
9  
3 
Process and 
Plant hazards: Physical hazards- 
Atmospheric 
contaminants, Sound, Light, Radiation, Pressure, and Temperature. 
9  

 
 
Electrical 
hazards-electric 
shock, 
flashover, 
lightning 
Strokes. 
Mechanical hazards. Environmental hazards. 
Human Errors-People Oriented Errors, Situation Oriented errors, 
System oriented errors. 
4 
Prevention techniques for hazards. Hazardous area classification. 
Safety in transportation of hazardous chemicals by road-HAZCHEM 
CODE, TREM CARD Relief system and Detectors. Flame arrester sand 
Flare system. 
Hazard rating of chemical plants- Dow fire, explosion and Toxicity 
index. Chemical exposure index. Emergency planning-onsite and offsite 
emergency planning, Mock drill. 
Hazard identification and Risk: HAZOP, Bow tie diagram, Fault tree 
analysis, failure mode and effect analysis, Eventtree analysis ,Layer of 
protection analysis. Examples. 
9

SEMESTER: S7 
POLYMERS & PHOTOVOLTAIC TECHNOLOGY 
Course Code 
PEPOT757 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3

2 Hrs. 30 Min.
